     <h1>
      Copyediting-L
     </h1>
     <p style="margin-left: 20px; margin-right: 20px">
      Copyediting-L is an email discussion list for editors and other defenders of the English language who want to talk about anything related to editing: sticky style issues; philosophy of editing; newspaper, technical, and other specialized editing; reference books; client relations; Internet resources; electronic editing and software; freelance issues; and so on.
      <a href="http://www.RobertsIndexing.com">
       Carol Roberts
      </a>
      started the list at Cornell University in December 1992 and passed ownership of the list to Beth Goelzer Lyons. Bill Blinn and Jane Lyle became the list owners in the late 1990s. At the end of 2013, they turned ownership over to
      <a href="mailto:editor@kokedit.com">
       Katharine O'Moore-Klopf
      </a>
      and John Renish. Katharine became the sole list owner in February 2016.
     </p>
     <p style="margin-left: 20px; margin-right: 20px">
      <strong>
       <em>
        Note:
       </em>
      </strong>
      If you are looking for a freelance editor, see the listings on the "Freelance" tab of this website. You will have to skim the information there to find contact details for individual editors you'd like to contact about your project. There is no main person who supervises the individuals listed there, because each person there is an independent contractor.
      <em>
       <strong>
        Copyediting-L is not an editing service or business and does not employ anyone. Copyediting-L also is not a professional association for editors; it is an email discussion list only. There are no annual dues.
       </strong>
      </em>
     </p>
     <p style="margin-left: 20px; margin-right: 20px">
      We have two lists:
      <strong>
       Copyediting-L
      </strong>
      (nicknamed
      <em>
       CE-L
      </em>
      ) is the main list, where topics such as politics, religion, sex, and operating-system evangelism are forbidden.
      <strong>
       Copyediting-Off-list-L
      </strong>
      (nicknamed
      <em>
       CEL-O
      </em>
      ) is the "chat" list, where all topics are permitted. Subscribing to the off-list requires that you be already subscribed to the main list.
     </p>
     <p style="margin-left: 20px; margin-right: 20px">
      <strong>
       Both lists
       <font color="#CC0000">
        explicitly forbid personal attacks and commercial posts
       </font>
       (
       <em>
        that is, do not post to promote your editing business or availability for projects
       </em>
       ). Before you begin posting to the list, please read all of the material under the "FAQ" tab. Please
       <em>
        also
       </em>
       lurk for a few days to get a sense of list norms.
      </strong>
     </p>
     <p style="margin-left: 20px; margin-right: 20px">
      The Copyediting-L (CE-L) archive:
      <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-l" target="_blank">
       https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-l
      </a>
     </p>
     <p style="margin-left: 20px; margin-right: 20px">
      The Copyediting-Off-List-L (CEL-O) archive:
      <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l" target="_blank">
       https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l
      </a>
     </p>

       <h3>
        How to Subscribe
       </h3>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Create a new blank e-mail message addressed to
         <a href="mailto:iulist@iulist.indiana.edu">
          iulist@iulist.indiana.edu
         </a>
         .
        </li>
        <li>
         Choose the list you want to subscribe to:
         <ul>
          <li>
           <strong>
            COPYEDITING-L
           </strong>
           (editing-related topics):
           <br/>
           Leave the message blank and type the following in the
           <strong>
            subject
           </strong>
           line:
           <strong>
            <br/>
            subscribe copyediting-l Firstname Lastname
           </strong>
           <br/>
           Where ...
           <br/>
           <strong>
            -l
           </strong>
           is a dash (aka "hyphen") and the lowercase letter "L", not the numeral "1".
           <br/>
           <strong>
            Firstname
           </strong>
           is your first name.
           <br/>
           <strong>
            Lastname
           </strong>
           is your last name.
          </li>
          <li>
           <strong>
            COPYEDITING-OFF-LIST-L
           </strong>
           (non-editing-related discussions):
           <br/>
           <em>
            Only Copyediting-L subscribers may subscribe to the off-list.
           </em>
           <br/>
           Leave the message blank and type the following in the
           <strong>
            subject
           </strong>
           line:
           <strong>
            <br/>
            subscribe copyediting-off-list-l Firstname Lastname
           </strong>
           <br/>
           Where ...
           <br/>
           <strong>
            -l
           </strong>
           is a dash (aka "hyphen") and the lowercase letter "L", not the numeral "1".
           <br/>
           <strong>
            Firstname
           </strong>
           is your first name.
           <br/>
           <strong>
            Lastname
           </strong>
           is your last name.
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li>
         Send the message. You will receive a response from the Sympa server, and then you must confirm your desire to subscribe to the list by doing one of the following:
         <ul>
          <li>
           Replying to the message
          </li>
          <li>
           Sending a message with the authorization text in the subject line to the Sympa server
          </li>
          <li>
           Clicking a link in the message to create a confirmation message and then sending it
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li>
         The server will respond with a welcome message. You are now subscribed.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h3>
        How to Unsubscribe
       </h3>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Create a new blank e-mail message addressed to
         <a href="mailto:iulist@iulist.indiana.edu">
          iulist@iulist.indiana.edu
         </a>
         .
        </li>
        <li>
         Choose the list you want to unsubscribe from:
         <ul>
          <li>
           <strong>
            COPYEDITING-L
           </strong>
           (editing-related topics):
           <br/>
           Leave the message blank and type the following in the
           <strong>
            subject
           </strong>
           line:
           <strong>
            <br/>
            unsubscribe copyediting-l
           </strong>
           <br/>
           Note that
           <strong>
            -l
           </strong>
           is a hyphen plus the lowercase letter "L", not the numeral "1".
           <br/>
          </li>
          <li>
           <strong>
            COPYEDITING-OFF-LIST-L
           </strong>
           (non-editing-related discussions):
           <br/>
           Leave the message blank and type the following in the
           <strong>
            subject
           </strong>
           line:
           <strong>
            <br/>
            unsubscribe copyediting-off-list-l
           </strong>
           <br/>
           Note that
           <strong>
            -l
           </strong>
           is a hyphen plus the lowercase letter "L", not the numeral "1".
           <br/>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li>
         Send the message. You will receive a confirmation message from the Sympa server.
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>

       </title>

       <p>
        Yes, it's true that this isn't structured as a traditional FAQ, but it's intended to serve the same purpose.
       </p>
       <h1>
        Introduction to Copyediting-L
       </h1>
       <p>
        IMPORTANT: In April 2012, Copyediting-L (CE-L) and Copyediting-Off-list-L (CEL-O) were migrated from Indiana University's Listserv server to a new Sympa server.
       </p>
       <p>
        For GENERAL INFORMATION about Sympa, see the
        <a href="https://iulist.indiana.edu/sympa/help/user" target="blank">
         IU List Service Help Page
        </a>
        . A description of all the commands you can send to Sympa is available on the
        <a href="https://iulist.indiana.edu/sympa/help/mail_commands" target="_blank">
         Commands page
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <br/>
       <div h4="" style="border:2px dotted black;padding:1em;">
        <font color="#CC0000">
         <strong>
          Before posting, please read this section.
         </strong>
        </font>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <em>
           Copyediting-L is not an editing service or business and does not employ anyone. Copyediting-L also is not a professional association for editors; it is an email discussion list only. There are no annual dues. We do not maintain a directory of members, although we do maintain a list of subscribers who are freelancers (see the "Freelancers" tab on this website).
          </em>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <p>
         By reading or posting messages to Copyediting-L (aka CE-L), you agree that CE-L's list owners and members cannot be held responsible for any damage caused by this system. This includes, but is not limited to, damage caused by its users, hackers, and hardware or software failures. There is no guarantee of reliable service or security of information. All information placed on CE-L is to be considered public. While we do our best to stop inappropriate use of the list and harassment, we cannot prevent it entirely. List owners reserve the right to limit posting, suspend accounts, or deny access to anyone at any time. List owners will never ask you for your password; anyone who does so is a fraud.
        </p>
        <p>
         Copyediting-L uses a tagging system to categorize messages so that non-digest subscribers can include or exclude specific topics. All posts should have an identifying tag in the subject line, and tags must be spelled and punctuated precisely. (You have to type the tag in yourself; there is no automation for adding a tag. For additional information on tags, see the heads
         <a href="#SubjectLines">
          "Subject Lines and Tags"
         </a>
         and
         <a href="#Valid">
          "Valid Tags"
         </a>
         below.) There is also an auxiliary "off-list" list (Copyediting-Off-list-L) for discussions not directly related to editing.
        </p>
        <p>
         Copyediting-L is a busy list. We recommend that you choose to receive individual messages because this allows you to filter the list mail based on the tags that subscribers use in their subject lines. Subscribers who choose the digest format always receive all messages posted to the list.
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          Please quote sparingly.
         </strong>
         As editors, we should be able to trim quoted material to include only the essential parts. When a post includes a long and involved explanation to set the stage for a question, there is no need for respondents to repeat the introduction in their answer. Those who quote excessively will receive reminders from a list owner; continued excessive quoting may result in posting limitations.
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          Respect each other.
         </strong>
         Diversity in editing and opinions about editing is encouraged. Civilized argumentation and debate are fine. Character digs, personal attacks, and inflammatory language are
         <em>
          not
         </em>
         . You are responsible for what you write. Those who cannot be civil will be removed from the list.
        </p>
       </div>
       <a name="Resources">
        <h2>
         Online Resources
        </h2>
       </a>
       <p>
        The Copyediting-L (CE-L) archive:
        <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-l" target="_blank">
         https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-l
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        The Copyediting-Off-List-L (CEL-O) archive:
        <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l" target="_blank">
         https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Access to the archives is limited to subscribers. You must log in to view the archives.
        </strong>
        If you have not previously created a password, click the "
        <em>
         First Login
        </em>
        " link in the upper left corner. Then on the page you are taken to, look for the "
        <em>
         First login?
        </em>
        " link. Click it. On the new page that you are taken to, type in the email address that you are subscribed under, and then click the "
        <em>
         Request first password
        </em>
        " button. Follow the instructions in the automated email that you will receive.
       </p>
       <a name="Privacy">
        <h2>
         Privacy
        </h2>
       </a>
       <p>
        CE-L and CEL-O are set up so that only the list owners can see the names and e-mail addresses in the list of subscribers. Other subscribers will, of course, see your name and e-mail address when you post messages. The archives are available only to subscribers.
        <em>
         This does not mean that what you post to the list is private.
        </em>
        Anyone may join the list, and subscribers may forward your messages to others. Don't post anything that you wouldn't want your parents, your life partner, your children, your extended family, your neighbors, your immediate supervisor, your coworkers, or your clients to read.
       </p>

       <h1>
        <a name="GeneralInfo">
        </a>
        General Information
       </h1>
       <p>
        In December 1992, Carol Roberts started this list at Cornell University. The second list owner was Beth Goelzer Lyons. Bill Blinn and Jane Lyle served as list co-owners from the late 1990s through 2013. Katharine O'Moore-Klopf and John Renish became the list co-owners at the end of 2013, and then Katharine became the sole list owner in February 2016.
       </p>
       <p>
        Subsequent references to
        <em>
         Copyediting-L
        </em>
        also apply to
        <em>
         Copyediting-Off-List-L
        </em>
        except when specified otherwise.
       </p>
       <p>
        Copyediting-L is an unmoderated list, which means that your posts are sent to the list immediately without being reviewed by a list owner.
        <font color="#CC0000">
         <strong>
          However, subscribers who engage in unacceptable behavior may be placed on moderated status or removed from the list.
         </strong>
        </font>
       </p>
       <p>
        The default mail setting is digest, which means that you will receive one or more digests. All digests from the previous day are sent at 6 a.m. Eastern time. Digests are not edited or condensed. To make the list posts easier to manage and to improve timeliness, the list owners enthusiastically recommend changing your account settings to receive individual messages. See "Managing Your Subscription (Subscribe, Unsubscribe, Etc.)" to learn how to make changes to your subscription, including unsubscribing.
       </p>
       <p>
        Only subscribers can send messages to Copyediting-L. If the address you use to send mail varies in any way from the address you used when you subscribed, the server will not recognize you as a subscriber. Contact the list owners for help.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Copyright restrictions
        </strong>
        apply to all Copyediting-L and Copyediting-Off-list-L material, including the archives and this document. Copyediting-L and Copyediting-Off-list-L material may not be used anywhere online, or in material to be published in any manner, without the permission of the author or authors, who retain full copyright to their words, and without crediting the author or authors. Even if you believe that reposting elsewhere a snippet of someone's post from either email list might constitute fair use under U.S. copyright laws, you are expected, as a condition of remaining a subscriber to the lists, to obtain permission from the original poster or posters before reposting the information—with credit to the source(s)—elsewhere. The reason for this condition is that what constitutes fair use is open to interpretation. If you cannot obtain permission from an author, do not use their material from Copyediting-L or Copyediting-Off-list-L.
       </p>
       <p>
        <em>
         If you engage in a private (offlist) discussion with a listmate, do not then quote anything from that discussion without first obtaining the author's permission to include the material in messages that you post to Copyediting-L or Copyediting-Off-list-L.
        </em>
       </p>
       <p>
        For information on U.S. copyright law, see the appropriate section of the website of the
        <a href="http://www.copyright.gov/title17/" target="_blank">
         United States Copyright Office
        </a>
        . For information on fair use, see the
        <a href="http://www.copyright.gov/fair-use/" target="_blank">
         U.S. Copyright Office Fair Use Index
        </a>
        online.
       </p>
       <p>
        These guidelines are subject to interpretation by the list owners, who make every effort to apply them consistently and fairly. Those who fail to comply with the guidelines will receive off-list reminders and, if inappropriate posts continue, may have their posting rights restricted, suspended, or revoked.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="#TableContents">
         <em>
          Return to Table of Contents
         </em>
        </a>
       </p>
       <h1>
        <a name="GuidelinesFor">
        </a>
        Guidelines for Posting to the List
       </h1>
       <ul>
        <li>
         To send a message to the main list, use this address:
         <a href="/mailto:copyediting-l@indiana.edu">
          copyediting-l@indiana.edu
         </a>
         .
        </li>
        <li>
         To send a message to the off-list, use this address:
         <a href="/mailto:copyediting-off-list-l@indiana.edu">
          copyediting-off-list-l@indiana.edu
         </a>
         .
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Please keep messages as short as possible.
        </strong>
        CE-L is a busy list, and needlessly long messages are tedious.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         When replying to a message,  keep only as much of the original text as is necessary to frame your reply.
        </strong>
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Use a descriptive subject line with the appropriate tag.
        </strong>
        Many people use the subject line to decide whether they want to read a message, and some use the tags to filter messages. See "Subject Lines and Tags" for details.
       </p>
       <p>
        Copyright restrictions apply. Provide a complete bibliographic citation for all copyrighted materials and obtain permission as required from the original author before posting.
       </p>
       <p>
        Poll or survey questions (Example: "How many of you ...?") are permitted on the list, but those who ask such questions should request that all responses be sent to them privately. It is their responsibility to compile the responses and provide a brief summary to the list.
       </p>
       <h2>
        <a name="Topics">
         Inappropriate Topics
        </a>
       </h2>
       <p>
        Political comments are not permitted on the main list. The Internet is home to many political discussion lists, but CE-L is not one of them. Evangelizing for Windows, Mac, or Linux platforms is unwelcome. Choose your computing platform, your religion (or lack thereof), your word processor, and your pet to suit yourself. Allow others to choose theirs.
       </p>
       <p>
        Posts reporting minor typos in publications or mispronunciations by radio or television personalities are not appropriate. People have been confusing "libery" with "library," "Febuary" with "February," and "Calvary" with "cavalry" since these words entered the language. Likewise, grocery store signs using "it's" as a possessive are singularly unremarkable. The planet Earth is surrounded by air, but most of us do not find this fact to be worthy of comment.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Advertisements are forbidden, whether for your own services or the services of others. Do not request referrals onlist.
        </strong>
        Brief (up to 10 lines) "help wanted" ads are allowed if you include off-list contact information. Brief (up to 10 lines) announcements of editing-related conferences, seminars, and meetings that are open to non-members are also allowed if you include off-list contact information. Do not post an entire conference schedule, and do not post the announcement more than once.
       </p>
       <p>
        Do not post a question that can be unequivocally answered by consulting a dictionary, the
        <em>
         Chicago Manual of Style
        </em>
        , the
        <em>
         AP Stylebook
        </em>
        , or any other common reference. Questions about variations in the answers provided by those references, as well as questions about interpretations, are welcome.
       </p>
       <p>
        Do not point out grammar or spelling mistakes in messages unless the author has explicitly asked for such advice. We are all human. We all commit typos.
        <font color="#CC0000">
         <strong>
          In short: Respect each other. Diversity in editing and opinions about editing is encouraged. Civilized argumentation and debate are fine. Character digs, personal attacks, and inflammatory language are
          <em>
           not
          </em>
          . You are responsible for what you write. Those who cannot be civil will be removed from the list.
         </strong>
        </font>
       </p>
       <p>
        Avoid posting messages from other lists. If you have a list of one-liners that you want to share, post three or four of them to CEL-O (not to CE-L) and offer to send the full list to those who contact you privately. If you've received an e-zine or e-mail that contains information you feel would be helpful to others, describe it and provide a link to the original or offer the full message to those who request it.
       </p>
       <p>
        Do not post urban legends or virus warnings.
       </p>
       <p>
        While it might seem unfriendly or even rude, we discourage posting thank-you messages to the list. CE-L subscribers tend to be generous in sharing their knowledge and expertise, and if everyone thanked each person who helped, about half of the list traffic would be thank-you notes. Unless someone has gone to extreme measures to help you, please send thank-you messages privately.
       </p>
       <p>
        If you are traveling and would like to meet CE-L subscribers in your destination city, post a message to the list and indicate the dates you will be in the other city. Follow-up arrangements should be made off-list.
       </p>
       <h2>
        <a name="IncludingURL">
        </a>
        Including a URL in Your Post
       </h2>
       <p>
        If you place a URL in your post, please also include information about where the URL leads and why CE-L subscribers would want to go there. Post the full URL inside
        <em>
         greater than
        </em>
        and
        <em>
         less than
        </em>
        symbols. Example:
        <br/>
        <span class="urldemo">
         &lt;www.copyediting-l.info&gt;
        </span>
        or
        <span class="urldemo">
         &lt;http://www.copyediting-l.info&gt;
        </span>
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Please be sure to include &lt; and &gt;, and do not use a URL-shortening service.
        </strong>
        After several years of explaining to people that URL-shortening services such as bit.ly, tinyurl.com, and goo.gl would help communicate URLs that are long enough to break across lines, we must now take the opposite approach because certain system administrators have concluded that these services are evil and thus may reject messages that contain shortened URLs or blacklist email addresses that are known to send messages containing shortened URLs.
       </p>
       <h2>
        <a name="Shorthand">
        </a>
        CE-L Shorthand
       </h2>
       <p>
        You may occasionally see some unfamiliar terms in CE-L posts. For example:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <strong>
          CE-L
         </strong>
         = Copyediting-L
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          The CE-Lery
         </strong>
         = All Copyediting-L listmates collectively (a vegetable joke based on the nickname
         <em>
          CE-L
         </em>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          CEL-O
         </strong>
         = Copyediting-Off-List-L
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          Fe
         </strong>
         = irony or sarcasm (Fe is the chemical symbol for iron)
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          Stalks
         </strong>
         = All Copyediting-L listmates collectively (a vegetable joke based on the nickname
         <em>
          CE-Lery
         </em>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          Stitch
         </strong>
         = Referring to another thread (another topic under discussion) on Copyediting-L
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          TIA
         </strong>
         or
         <strong>
          Spanish aunt
         </strong>
         (
         <em>
          aunt
         </em>
         in Spanish is
         <em>
          tia
         </em>
         ) = "Thanks in advance"
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h2>
        <a name="AvoidExcessive">
        </a>
        Avoid Excessive Quoting
       </h2>
       <p>
        The number one bothersome trait the list owners hear about fairly regularly is excessive quoting. Questions often contain additional information that makes the question complete and detailed. Much of this extra information need not be (and should not be) quoted in the reply.
       </p>
       <p>
        For CE-L subscribers who receive digests instead of individual messages, excessive quoting is even more troublesome.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <a name="Summarizing">
         Summarizing Is a Good Choice
        </a>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Some subscribers summarize the question succinctly instead of quoting. This takes extra time and effort, but it substantially reduces list clutter. We don't all have the time or the inclination to summarize, but we should all at least be able to edit the quoted material to omit those parts that have little bearing on the answer.
       </p>
       <p>
        Before sending a message to the list, please examine it.
       </p>
       <ol>
        <li>
         Have you deleted (at the very least) the original sender's signature and the archive tag line?
        </li>
        <li>
         Have you left more of the original text than is necessary for readers to understand what you're responding to?
        </li>
       </ol>
       <p>
        If the quoted text is longer than your reply, please examine the message again with particular attention to point 2.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="#TableContents">
         <em>
          Return to Table of Contents
         </em>
        </a>
       </p>
       <h1>
        <a name="SubjectLines">
        </a>
        Subject Lines and Tags
       </h1>
       <p>
        No message is complete until it has a tag and a descriptive subject line. No new topic should ever begin with the CHAT tag. Tags may be written in upper case, lower case, or mixed case.
       </p>
       <p>
        Before sending either an original message or a reply to someone else's message, glance at the subject line to confirm that the tag and the descriptive subject are properly formatted and appropriate to the subject matter. If you are replying to a message that has no tag or an incorrect tag, please add or correct the tag. You have to type the tag in yourself; there is no automation for adding a tag.
       </p>
       <p>
        <em>
         <strong>
          Here is some clarification about terminology:
         </strong>
        </em>
       </p>
       <p>
        CE-L message subject lines carry
        <em>
         both
        </em>
        a subject-line tag
        <em>
         and
        </em>
        an email list identifier.
       </p>
       <p>
        <font color="#CC0000">
         [CE-L]
        </font>
        is NOT a subject-line tag.
        <font color="#CC0000">
         [CE-L]
        </font>
        is the email list identifier that the list software prepends to each message's subject line before delivering the message to the entire list. The software is set up to do that because many different email lists use the software, and the identifier helps readers keep straight which list's emails they are reading.
       </p>
       <p>
        You will see, in subject lines that listmates have handled correctly, both the [CE-L] list identifier AND a subject-matter tag. For example, take a look at the following subject line of a message:
       </p>
       <font color="#CC0000">
        <strong>
         [CE-L] USAGE: Subjunctive mood
        </strong>
       </font>
       <p>
       </p>
       <p>
        <font color="#CC0000">
         USAGE:
        </font>
        is the subject-line tag that the CE-L member typed with her own fingers before clicking Send on the message.
        <font color="#CC0000">
         [CE-L]
        </font>
        is the email identifier that was added
        <em>
         by the email list software
        </em>
        to the subject line after the CE-L member clicked Send on her message.
       </p>
       <p>
        You, as an email sender to Copyediting-L, must type in a tag yourself before sending out a message. You do not
        <em>
         ever
        </em>
        have to type in the email list identifier
        <font color="#CC0000">
         [CE-L]
        </font>
        in your message's subject line.
        <em>
         You will not see the server prepend
         <font color="#CC0000">
          [CE-L]
         </font>
         as it is happening. The server does this after you send your message and before it distributes your message to the email list.
        </em>
       </p>
       <p>
        Tags must be spelled exactly as shown below. Please note that JOB-OP has a hyphen between the two words. The tag must be followed by a colon. The colon must be followed by a space. The space is then followed by the subject. Example:
       </p>
       <p>
        <font color="#CC0000">
         <strong>
          USAGE: A properly formatted subject line
         </strong>
        </font>
       </p>
       <p>
        Do
        <strong>
         not
        </strong>
        add square brackets, parentheses, or anything else around tags. They should
        <strong>
         only
        </strong>
        be followed by a colon and a word space.
       </p>
       <p>
        The server will add
        <font color="#CC0000">
         [CE-L]
        </font>
        or
        <font color="#CC0000">
         [CEL-O]
        </font>
        to the left of the tag.
        <em>
         You will not see this as it is happening. The server does this after you send your message and before it distributes your message to the email list.
        </em>
        Please do not add this on your own.
       </p>
       <p>
        Except for CHAT, tags may be combined. This should be done sparingly, though, and CHAT should never be combined with any other tag. No topic should ever begin with a CHAT tag. If the topic is so far afield that the first post would require that it be labeled CHAT, then the message belongs on CEL-O, not on CE-L.
       </p>
       <p>
        URGENT is not a tag. If you need a prompt answer, place the word "URGENT" in the descriptive subject section. Example:
        <br/>
        <br/>
        QUERY URGENT: This is
        <em>
         incorrect
        </em>
        <br/>
        QUERY: URGENT This is correct
       </p>
       <p>
        STYLE is
        <em>
         not
        </em>
        a tag. Please do not use it as a tag.
       </p>
       <p>
        If you write a message starting a new discussion and forget to add a tag to the Subject line before you click Send, please do
        <strong>
         not
        </strong>
        re-send the message with a tag added. Just make sure to add a tag to the Subject line of any replies that you send.
       </p>
       <p>
        If you reply to a message for which the original poster forgot to include a tag, please
        <strong>
         do
        </strong>
        add a tag to the Subject line before you click Send.
       </p>
       <p>
        You have to type the tag in yourself; there is no automation for adding a tag.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="#TableContents">
         <em>
          Return to Table of Contents
         </em>
        </a>
       </p>
       <h2>
        <a name="Valid">
         Valid Tags
        </a>
       </h2>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <strong>
          ADMIN:
         </strong>
         List owner use ONLY. If you reply to an ADMIN message on-list, please change the tag.
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          BIZ:
         </strong>
         Business practices, rates (limited, please), journalism, media, etc.
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          CHAT:
         </strong>
         As threads mutate from their original topic, posters may use the CHAT tag, but the discussion should continue on CEL-O. Exception: The occasional pun war is a part of CE-L's heritage and may be continued on the main list. Pun wars are usually of short duration.
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          CONF:
         </strong>
         Short (10 lines maximum, preferably less) announcements about upcoming conferences and other programs of interest to editors. Always provide a link to more information. Only one post per event is permitted.
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          JOB-OP:
         </strong>
         Job opportunities. No advertisements, "position wanted," or "referrals wanted" messages are allowed. These should be short messages (approximately 10 lines in length) and should include a link to a website with full information.
         <em>
          Note the hyphen in the tag. It is required.
         </em>
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          MISC:
         </strong>
         Anything that doesn't fit a standard category.
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          QUERY:
         </strong>
         Editing questions not related to grammar and style.
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          SUMMARY:
         </strong>
         Use this tag when you report information that you have collected off-list in response to a query.
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          TOOLS:
         </strong>
         Hardware and software, books, desks, pencils, and anything else an editor might need.
        </li>
        <li>
         <strong>
          USAGE:
         </strong>
         Grammar and style issues. Note that USAGE covers both
         <em>
          grammar
         </em>
         and
         <em>
          style
         </em>
         , neither of which is a tag in its own right.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        If you cannot decide between two tags, you may combine them by typing one tag, a space, the second tag, and then a colon. Please do this sparingly and keep in mind that CHAT should never be used with any other tag. Dual tags follow this format:
        <br/>
        TAG TAG: Descriptive subject
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="#TableContents">
         <em>
          Return to Table of Contents
         </em>
        </a>
       </p>
       <h1>
        <a name="ManagingSub">
        </a>
        Managing Your Subscription
       </h1>
       <h1>
        (Subscribe, Unsubscribe, Etc.)
       </h1>
       <p>
        Copyediting-L is located at the center of the self-service section of the Internet. You are expected to manage your own subscription either via the Web interface, which is largely self-documenting, or by e-mail. When sending a single command to the server, it should be placed on the subject line. Sending multiple-line commands is possible but the message must be entirely plain text and without a signature.
        <a href="https://iulist.indiana.edu/sympa/help/user" target="_blank">
         An explanation of how to send multiple-line commands is on the IU website
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Because Sympa is a computer program, you must follow the single-command format
        <em>
         exactly
        </em>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Send your message from your email address (the one that you used for subscribing to the list) to
        <em>
         iulist@iulist.indiana.edu
        </em>
        . Place your command on the subject line of the message (not in the message body). In the command, type the appropriate command (e.g.,
        <em>
         unsubscribe
        </em>
        ) from the bulleted list below, followed by either
        <em>
         copyediting-l
        </em>
        or
        <em>
         copyediting-off-list-l
        </em>
        (depending on which list you are dealing with), and then your first name (shown as Firstname in the following examples) and your last name (shown as Lastname in the following examples). Note that in the following examples,
        <em>
         {list}
        </em>
        is simply a placeholder for the name of the list (
        <em>
         copyediting-l
        </em>
        or
        <em>
         copyediting-off-list-l
        </em>
        ) that you will type in. Please delete that placeholder before you send your message.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Example: unsubscribe copyediting-off-list-l
        </strong>
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Subscription status command (list of all lists you are subscribed to):
         <br/>
         <span class="command">
          which
         </span>
        </li>
        <li>
         Subscribe command:
         <br/>
         <span class="command">
          subscribe {list} Firstname Lastname
         </span>
        </li>
        <li>
         Unsubscribe command:
         <br/>
         <span class="command">
          unsubscribe {list}
         </span>
        </li>
        <li>
         Set digest mode command (this is the default):
         <br/>
         <span class="command">
          set {list} digest
         </span>
        </li>
        <li>
         Set individual messages mode command:
         <br/>
         <span class="command">
          set {list} mail
         </span>
        </li>
        <li>
         Temporarily stop receiving messages (when you're busy or on vacation) command:
         <br/>
         <span class="command">
          set {list} nomail
         </span>
         <br/>
         Existing subscribers who inadvertently unsubscribe instead of using the "nomail" option will go through the new-subscriber process each time they leave and return.
        </li>
        <li>
         Start receiving messages again command:
         <br/>
         <span class="command">
          set {list} mail
          <br/>
          set {list} digest
         </span>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        The Copyediting-L (CE-L) archive:
        <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-l" target="_blank">
         https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-l
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        The Copyediting-Off-List-L (CEL-O) archive:
        <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l" target="_blank">
         https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l
        </a>
       </p>
       <h2>
        <a name="Selecting">
         Selecting Topics for Individual Messages
        </a>
       </h2>
       <p>
        If you choose to receive individual messages, you may specify which topics you want to receive. Those who subscribe to the digest will always receive all messages. This does not apply to the off-list because no tags are used there. Selecting topics can be done via the
        <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l" target="_blank">
         Web interface
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         After logging in, select Subscriber Options from the left column.
        </li>
        <li>
         Check the topics that you wish to include in your subscription.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        <a href="#TableContents">
         <em>
          Return to Table of Contents
         </em>
        </a>
       </p>
       <h1>
        <a name="AddingYourself">
         Adding Yourself to the Directory of CE-L Freelancers
        </a>
       </h1>
       <p>
        As a service to Copyediting-L subscribers, Ann Fothergill-Brown (
        <a href="/MAILTO:celery.free@gmail.com">
         celery.free@gmail.com
        </a>
        ) maintains a directory of freelancers (part-time and full-time). The list is on the Copyediting-L information website (
        <a href="http://www.copyediting-l.info">
         http://www.copyediting-l.info
        </a>
        ), and Ann sends it privately to anyone on request. Keep in mind that there is no control over what happens to the list once it is posted. To be added to the list, you must be a Copyediting-L subscriber, and you must submit a request that adheres to the process outlined on the "Freelancers" tab.
       </p>
       <p>
        To add yourself to the list, send a message to
        <a href="/mailto:celery.free@gmail.com">
         celery.free@gmail.com
        </a>
        and use the format specified below. Those who fail to follow the format will not be listed.
       </p>
       <blockquote>
        <p>
         Doe, Jean
         <br/>
         100 Elm St., City, State/Province, Zip/Postal Code, Country
         <br/>
         jdoe@example.com
         <br/>
         607-555-1212 (fax 607-555-1313)
         <br/>
         Type of work: Copyediting, proofreading, indexing
         <br/>
         Type of materials: Books, journals, manuals, technical materials
         <br/>
         Experience: Since 1950
         <br/>
         Subjects: Business, computers, mathematics, natural resources
        </p>
       </blockquote>
       <p>
        <em>
         Note: If you unsubscribe from Copyediting-L, your directory entry will be deleted.
        </em>
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="#TableContents">
         <em>
          Return to Table of Contents
         </em>
        </a>
       </p>
       <h1>
        <a name="Archives">
        </a>
        The Archives
       </h1>
       <p>
        The Web interface for each list gives you access to the archives. The archives are closed to non-subscribers, but users should keep in mind that anything posted to the lists is potentially visible to everyone in the world.
       </p>
       <p>
        The Copyediting-L (CE-L) archive:
        <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-l" target="_blank">
         https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-l
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        The Copyediting-Off-List-L (CEL-O) archive:
        <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l" target="_blank">
         https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        The first time you use the Web interface, you will be asked to enter your password. If you haven't yet set one up, you can do so from that screen. You will need to enter the e-mail address from which you are subscribed and then type a password. The server will send a message to the e-mail address you gave it, and you must reply to that message to confirm that you are who you say you are.
       </p>
       <p>
        Once you have successfully established a password, the server will offer to write a
        <em>
         cookie
        </em>
        to your computer. This will save the password on your computer so that you will not need to enter it again from that machine. If you use other computers, you will need to enter the password once from each location to create the cookie.
       </p>
       <p>
        To search the archives, select the Search Archives option.
        <br/>
        <img alt="Select Search" height="303" src="/images/Search1.png" width="618"/>
       </p>
       <p>
        Next, type the phrase you're looking for into the Search Archive text box. When specifying the phrase, do not place it inside quotation marks as you might do for a Google search. Before clicking Search, be sure to specify a date range. If you specify no range, the search will include only the most recent few months. Try to narrow the date range, though; selecting all dates may cause the search to time out on the server.
        <br/>
        <img alt="Select a date range" height="633" src="/images/Search2.png" width="630"/>
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="#TableContents">
         <em>
          Return to Table of Contents
         </em>
        </a>
       </p>
       <h1>
        <a name="CEL-OList">
         CEL-O, the Off-list List
        </a>
       </h1>
       <p>
        In 2002, we added CEL-O, the "off-list list," for use by those who want to discuss non-editing-related topics with other CE-L subscribers. Anyone wishing to subscribe to CEL-O must first subscribe to CE-L. New subscriptions must be approved by a list owner, who will confirm that the request is coming from a CE-L subscriber. The CEL-O archive is at
        <a href="https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l" target="_blank">
         https://list.indiana.edu/sympa/arc/copyediting-off-list-l
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        CEL-O runs on the same Sympa software that powers CE-L, so all of the standard list management commands described here apply. No topics are banned on CEL-O, but those who post excessively or who are abusive to others will be removed at the sole discretion of the list owners.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Never cross-post a message to both lists.
        </strong>
        However, if you want to start a discussion that is vaguely related to editing, you may post the original message to CE-L (and ONLY to CE-L) with a CHAT tag. Place this text at the TOP of the message: Please respond on CEL-O.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="#TableContents">
         <em>
          Return to Table of Contents
         </em>
        </a>
       </p>
       <h1>
        <a name="ContactingOwner">
        </a>
        Contacting a List Owner
       </h1>
       <p>
        Messages sent to the following address will reach a list owner:
        <br/>
       </p>
       <noscript>
        Please enable Javascript to see the address!
       </noscript>
       <script>
        var addr = 'copyediting-l-request';
var at = '@';
var dom = 'list.indiana';
var dot = '.';
var tld = 'edu';
document.write('<a href="mailto:');
document.write(addr + at + dom + dot + tld);
document.write('">');
document.write(addr + at + dom + dot + tld);
document.write('</a>');
       </script>

       <p>
        The resources available here have been provided by Copyediting-L (CE-L) subscribers because they are generous. If you find errors in any resource shared here, please remember that all editors—even highly experienced ones—are human beings and sometimes make mistakes.
       </p>
       <p>
        Many thanks to all of our contributors.
       </p>
       <br/>
       <h1>
        Microsoft Word Macros and Templates
       </h1>
       <p>
        If you would like to contribute a macro or template, send the file, or a link to it, to
        <script language="javascript">
         var atsign = '@';
var dot = '.';
document.write('<a href="mailto:' + 'editor' + atsign 
+ 'kokedit' + dot + 'com">');
        </script>
        Katharine O'Moore-Klopf for inclusion here.
       </p>
       <h5>
        From Karen Bojda:
       </h5>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a href="resources/KarenBojdaMacros.doc" target="_blank">
          Macros
         </a>
         (Word file)
        </li>

       <h5>
        From Paul Beverley:
       </h5>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a href="http://www.archivepub.co.uk/book.html" target="_blank">
          <em>
           Macros for Editors
          </em>
         </a>
         , a free and frequently updated 600-plus-page book of more than 500 macros for Microsoft Word
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC6J6ZPMJQ0T5eMIcX3tKh2g" target="_blank">
          Video tutorials
         </a>
         on using macros from the book
         <em>
          Macros for Editors
         </em>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h5>
        From Mark Fretz, via Scribe Inc.:
       </h5>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a href="https://scribenet.com/wfdw/sail" target="_blank">
          Scribe Add-In Lite ("SAI Lite")
         </a>
         , a free template developed for Microsoft Word. SAI Lite enables users to apply structure to a manuscript and define elements for publication. It includes a ribbon for applying Word styles that are based on a predefined list of elements. The elements correspond to Scribe Markup Language (ScML), a system used for defining structural elements, such as an A-level head or a block quotation, in a manuscript. The full ScML list with descriptions is available
         <a href="https://scribenet.com/wfdw/docs/scml" target="_blank">
          here
         </a>
         .
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h1>
        Contributed Style Guides
       </h1>
       <p>
        In August 2005, one subscriber asked for samples of style guides. Another wanted copies. Then another and another ... and another. Here is a collection of style guides contributed by CE-L subscribers. The list is in chronological order by date received.
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Susan Talmadge,
         <a href="http://www.mlanet.org/p/cm/ld/fid=198" target="_blank">
          <em>
           Medical Library Association Style Manual
          </em>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         Sudhin V K,
         <em>
          Managed Care Magazine
         </em>
         <a href="http://www.managedcaremag.com/MC-BH_Stylebook_1.0_Web.pdf" target="_blank">
          PDF
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         Andrea Zuercher,
         <em>
          Health Affairs
         </em>
         <a href="style/AZ_style_mar_04.pdf" target="_blank">
          PDF
         </a>
         .
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h1>
        Miscellaneous Resources
       </h1>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Ann Fothergill-Brown maintains the Directory of CE-L Freelancers and updates it frequently. You can access the directory by clicking the "Freelancers" tab on this website. Follow the instructions on that page to request addition of an entry or updates to it.
        </li>
        <li>
         In February 2015, Katharine O'Moore-Klopf shared a
         <a href="https://www.dropbox.com/sh/isusr3iy8au98dx/AACM1B4-bSBVDNL7TvG3RYUfa?dl=0" target="_blank">
          list of packagers and editing services
         </a>
         , with links to their websites (right-click on the file that you see within the folder at that link and "save as" to your computer). Check the folder periodically for an updated list.
        </li>
        <li>
         In July 2014, David Newmarch shared an Excel-based editing rate calculator that he created. In April 2016, he shared version 2.0. In March 2017, he shared
         <a href="resources/PriceCalc v 2.1.xlsx" target="_blank">
          version 2.1
         </a>
         (right-click and "save as"). The calculator allows the user to see the equivalent fee per hour, per page, or per 100 words according to manuscript length and the pages-per-hour editing level required. It will also let you assess a selected rate against your income needs. David says that the calculator is "more cleanly and logically structured and has an option (requested by one CE-L user) for quickly switching between bigger and smaller documents. And the currency is left unspecified so that it holds good for a wide range of currency options. Setting it to show rate per hundred words rather than rate per word was an easy way to accommodate what could otherwise be fractions of a cent in a per-word rate for higher-value currencies. The chief difference in version 2.1 is that there's a slightly more rational and useful distinction (factor of 5 rather than 10) when you toggle between calculation for smaller document sizes or larger document sizes."
        </li>
        <li>
         Diana Stirling's (2008) editing marks for PDF documents (Zip documents):
         <br/>
         <a href="resources/Red.zip" target="_blank">
          Red set
         </a>
         (with instructions; right-click and "save as")
         <br/>
         <a href="resources/Black.zip" target="_blank">
          Black set
         </a>
         (with instructions; right-click and "save as")
        </li>
        <li>
         In July 2000, Kathy Frost put together a 24-page editing checklist "from
  my experience, a few friends, and the wonderful generosity of my CEL-mates."
         <a href="images/checklist.pdf" target="_blank">
          That file is posted here in PDF format.
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         Bryna Fischer's checklist form for writers and editors is
         <a href="images/ChecklistFormByBrynaFischer.pdf" target="_blank">
          here
         </a>
         .
    (It's a tiny PDF.)
        </li>
        <li>
         The Copyeditors' Knowledge Base is available at
         <a href="http://www.kokedit.com/ckb.php" target="_blank">
          http://www.kokedit.com/ckb.php
         </a>
         . E-mail Katharine O'Moore-Klopf at
         <a href="mailto:editor@kokedit.com">
          editor@kokedit.com
         </a>
         if you have information to be added to it.
        </li>
        <li>
         <font color="#CC0000">

           CE-L Logos:

         </font>
         If you want to use the CE-L logo, you'll find various formats and sizes
         <a href="logo.html">
          here
         </a>
         . The logo should be used only to indicate that you are a CE-L subscriber.
        </li>

      <div id="tabs-4">
       <h2>
        Directory of CE-L Freelancers
       </h2>
       <p>
        As a service to its subscribers, Copyediting-L maintains this directory of freelancers (part-time and full-time).
        <strong>
         This page is updated monthly.
        </strong>
        Individuals and companies who employ freelancers may request a copy in text, RTF, 
	or Microsoft Word format by sending a request to
        <a href="mailto:celery.free@gmail.com">
         celery.free@gmail.com
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        You can search for freelancers by subject, region, type of materials, or skill by using the Find or Search command 
	of your browser to search this page. 
	You can also find new and revised listings by searching for the text "
        <span class="new">
         NEW!
        </span>
        " 
	or "
        <span class="revised">
         REVISED
        </span>
        ."
       </p>
       <p>
        This directory is a single HTML page. Please allow enough time, given your Internet connection, for the page to load fully.
       </p>
       <h4>
        If you are a freelancer AND a CE-L subscriber, you can be listed in the directory of CE-L freelancers. 
	Please follow these directions EXACTLY.
       </h4>
       <ol>
        <li>
         Send your email request to
         <a href="mailto:celery.free@gmail.com">
          celery.free@gmail.com
         </a>
         from the e-mail address 
			that you use to subscribe to CE-L; otherwise, your listing will NOT be included.
         <br/>
         (The contact address in your listing need not be the same as the sending address, 
			and the sending address, if different, will not appear in the listing.)
        </li>
        <li>
         Use "CE-L Directory Update" as the subject line. 
			(Messages are filtered based on this subject line, and messages not using it are summarily deleted.)
        </li>
        <li>
         Note in the beginning of the message body whether the listing is new or revised.
        </li>
        <li>
         Present the listing, following the format
         <strong>
          EXACTLY
         </strong>
         , including line headings followed by a colon 
			(type of work, experience, and such).
         <br/>
         The sample listing that follows can be copied and edited to insert your own details.
			Do not include information other than that outlined in the sample.
			You may omit any information that is not relevant or that you simply don’t care to provide.
			Look at how others have handled their entries in the directory.
        </li>
        <li>
         If revising an entry, please send a completely new one, not just the changed information.
        </li>
        <li>
         Send your message without attachments.
        </li>
        <li>
         Remember that this directory is publicly available on the Internet.
        </li>
        <li>
         Please PROOFREAD your entry.
        </li>
       </ol>
       <h4>
        Please follow this sample EXACTLY:
       </h4>
       <blockquote>
        <strong>
         Surname, Firstname
        </strong>
        <br/>
        Business Name (if any)
        <br/>
        Street Address, City, ST 12345 COUNTRY
        <br/>
        email@address.com and www.domainname.com
        <br/>
        800-111-3333 (voice), 800-222-4444 (cell)
        <br/>
        Type of work: Substantive editing, line editing, copyediting, translation (Romulan &lt;−&gt; Mongol) rewriting, indexing
        <br/>
        Type of material: Books, journals, articles, reports, web sites
        <br/>
        Experience: Since 1905 (freelance since 1925); since 1930 (academic indexing)
        <br/>
        [OR]
        <br/>
        Experience: Seven years
        <br/>
        Subjects: International affairs, social sciences, natural sciences
        <br/>
        Availability: Full-time freelance
       </blockquote>

       <h2>
        Submit your blog information
       </h2>
       <p>
        To submit your blog information for the Copyediting-L website, please do this (examine the example and make your submission look like the example):
       </p>
       <ol>
        <li>
         Create an email with the subject "CE-L blog".
        </li>
        <li>
         Format the body of the email this way:
         <br/>
         Your Name
         <br/>
         Blog Name: http://blog.url.com
         <br/>
         One sentence about the blog.
        </li>
        <li>
         Send the email to
         <script language="javascript">
          var atsign = '@';
var dot = '.';
document.write('<a href="mailto:' + 'editor' + atsign 
+ 'kokedit' + dot + 'com">');
         </script>
         Katharine O'Moore-Klopf.
        </li>
       </ol>
       <strong>
        Example (this is what your email requesting the addition of your blog should look like):
       </strong>
       <p>
        Gabriela Hernandez
       Yakkity Yak: http://yak.notarealurl.net
       Everything you've always wanted to know about yaks.
       </p>
       <p>
        Note that in the above example, "Gabriela" should be replaced with your actual first name, just as "Hernandez" should be replaced by your actual surname.
       </p>
       <p>
       </p>
       <p>
        If at any point you unsubscribe from Copyediting-L, your blog listing will be removed from "Blogs" tab at http://www.copyediting-l.info.
       </p>
